<p>In August 2016, it was announced the BBC would be creating a new magazine-style show for the Premier League entitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Premier_League_Show" title="The Premier League Show">The Premier League Show</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2018, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Video" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Video">Amazon Video</a> would televise 20 games per season in a three-year deal beginning in the 2019–20 season.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The telecasts will be produced by a partnership of <a href="/wiki/Tinopolis" title="Tinopolis">Sunset + Vine</a> and BT Sport.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Worldwide">Worldwide</span></h3>
<p>The Premier League is the most-watched football league in the world, broadcast in 212 territories to 643&#160;million homes and a potential TV audience of 4.7&#160;billion people,.<sup id="cite_ref-Worldviews_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Worldviews-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The Premier League's production arm, <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Productions" title="Premier League Productions">Premier League Productions</a>, is operated by <a href="/wiki/IMG_(company)" title="IMG (company)">IMG Productions</a> and produces all content for its international television partners.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Premier League is particularly popular in Asia, where it is the most widely distributed sports programme.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> In Australia, <a href="/wiki/Optus" title="Optus">Optus</a> telecommunications holds exclusive rights to the Premier League, providing live broadcasts and online access (<a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports" title="Fox Sports">Fox Sports</a> formerly held rights).<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In India, the matches are broadcast live on <a href="/wiki/STAR_Sports" class="mw-redirect" title="STAR Sports">STAR Sports</a>. In China, the broadcast rights were awarded to Super Sports in a six-year agreement that began in the 2013–14 season.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> As of the 2019–20 season, Canadian broadcast rights to the Premier League are owned by <a href="/wiki/DAZN" title="DAZN">DAZN</a>, after having been jointly owned by <a href="/wiki/Sportsnet" title="Sportsnet">Sportsnet</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Sports_Network" title="The Sports Network">TSN</a> from 2013-14.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Premier League is <a href="/wiki/English_football_on_television#United_States" title="English football on television">broadcast in the United States</a> through <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports" title="NBC Sports">NBC Sports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
Premier League viewership has increased rapidly, with NBC and NBCSN averaging a record 479,000 viewers in the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Premier_League" title="2014–15 Premier League">2014–15 season</a>, up 118% from <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Premier_League" title="2012–13 Premier League">2012–13</a> when coverage still aired on <a href="/wiki/Fox_Soccer" title="Fox Soccer">Fox Soccer</a> and <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>/<a href="/wiki/ESPN2" title="ESPN2">ESPN2</a> (220,000 viewers),<sup id="cite_ref-Sports_Media_Watch_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sports_Media_Watch-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> and NBC Sports has been widely praised for its coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-Sports_Media_Watch_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sports_Media_Watch-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> NBC Sports reached a six-year extension with the Premier League in 2015 to broadcast the league through the 2021–22 season in a deal valued at $1&#160;billion (£640&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-U.S.Value_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S.Value-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Between the 1998–99 season and the 2012–13 season, <a href="/wiki/Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann" title="Raidió Teilifís Éireann">RTÉ</a> broadcast highlights on <i><a href="/wiki/Premier_Soccer_Saturday" title="Premier Soccer Saturday">Premier Soccer Saturday</a></i> and occasionally <i>Premier Soccer Sunday</i>. Between the 2004–05 season and the 2006–07 season, RTÉ broadcast a live match on 15 Saturday afternoons with each match being called <i>Premiership Live</i>.
</p><p>The Premier League is broadcast by <a href="/wiki/SuperSport_(South_African_TV_channel)" title="SuperSport (South African TV channel)">SuperSport</a> across <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Widening_gap_with_lower_leagues">Widening gap with lower leagues</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Premier_League%E2%80%93Football_League_gulf" title="Premier League–Football League gulf">Premier League–Football League gulf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Parachute_and_Solidarity_Payments" class="mw-redirect" title="Premier League Parachute and Solidarity Payments">Premier League Parachute and Solidarity Payments</a></div>
<p>There has been an increasing gulf between the Premier League and the Football League. Since its split with the <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League" title="English Football League">Football League</a>, many established clubs in the Premier League have managed to distance themselves from their counterparts in lower leagues. Owing in large part to the disparity in revenue from television rights between the leagues,<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> many newly promoted teams have found it difficult to avoid relegation in their first season in the Premier League. In every season except <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_FA_Premier_League" title="2001–02 FA Premier League">2001–02</a>, 2011–12 and 2017–18, at least one Premier League newcomer has been relegated back to the Football League. In <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_FA_Premier_League" title="1997–98 FA Premier League">1997–98</a>, all three promoted clubs were relegated at the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Premier League distributes a portion of its television revenue to clubs that are relegated from the league in the form of "parachute payments". Starting with the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Premier_League" title="2013–14 Premier League">2013–14</a> season, these payments are in excess of £60&#160;million over four seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Sport_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Sport-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Though designed to help teams adjust to the loss of television revenues (the average Premier League team receives £55&#160;million<sup id="cite_ref-Mail_Sport_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mail_Sport-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> while the average <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Football League Championship</a> club receives £2&#160;million),<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Sport_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Sport-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> critics maintain that the payments actually widen the gap between teams that have reached the Premier League and those that have not,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> leading to the common occurrence of teams "<a href="/wiki/Premier_League%E2%80%93Football_League_gulf" title="Premier League–Football League gulf">bouncing back</a>" soon after their relegation. For some clubs who have failed to win immediate promotion back to the Premier League, financial problems, including in some cases <a href="/wiki/Administration_(British_football)" title="Administration (British football)">administration</a> or even liquidation have followed. Further relegations down the footballing ladder have ensued for several clubs unable to cope with the gap.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadiums">Stadiums</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_stadiums" title="List of Premier League stadiums">List of Premier League stadiums</a></div>
<p>As of the 2017–18 season, Premier League football has been played in 58 stadiums since the formation of the division.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_disaster" title="Hillsborough disaster">Hillsborough disaster</a> in 1989 and the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Report" title="Taylor Report">Taylor Report</a> saw a recommendation that standing terraces should be abolished. As a result, all stadiums in the Premier League are <a href="/wiki/All-seater" class="mw-redirect" title="All-seater">all-seater</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Since the formation of the Premier League, football grounds in England have seen constant improvements to capacity and facilities, with some clubs moving to new-build stadiums.<sup id="cite_ref-Matchmood_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Matchmood-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Nine stadiums that have seen Premier League football have now been demolished. The stadiums for the 2017–18 season show a large disparity in capacity. For example, <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, the temporary home of Tottenham Hotspur, has a capacity of 90,000 while <a href="/wiki/Dean_Court" title="Dean Court">Dean Court</a>, the home of <a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a>, has a capacity of 11,360.<sup id="cite_ref-where_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-where-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The combined total capacity of the Premier League in the 2017–18 season is 806,033 with an average capacity of 40,302.<sup id="cite_ref-where_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-where-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Stadium attendances are a significant source of regular income for Premier League clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> For the 2016–17 season, average attendances across the league clubs were 35,838 for Premier League matches with an aggregate attendance of 13,618,596.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> This represents an increase of 14,712 from the average attendance of 21,126 recorded in the Premier League's first season (1992–93).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> However, during the 1992–93 season, the capacities of most stadiums were reduced as clubs replaced terraces with seats in order to meet the <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Report" title="Taylor Report">Taylor Report</a>'s 1994–95 deadline for <a href="/wiki/All-seater_stadium" title="All-seater stadium">all-seater stadiums</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The Premier League's record average attendance of 36,144 was set during the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Premier_League" title="2007–08 Premier League">2007–08</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> This record was then beaten in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Premier_League" title="2013–14 Premier League">2013–14</a> season recording an average attendance of 36,695 with an attendance of just under 14&#160;million, the highest average in England's top flight since 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Managers">Managers</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_managers" title="List of Premier League managers">List of Premier League managers</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Manager_(association_football)" title="Manager (association football)">Managers</a> in the Premier League are involved in the day-to-day running of the team, including the training, team selection and player acquisition. Their influence varies from club-to-club and is related to the ownership of the club and the relationship of the manager with fans.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Managers are required to have a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Pro_Licence" title="UEFA Pro Licence">UEFA Pro Licence</a> which is the final coaching qualification available, and follows the completion of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> 'B' and 'A' Licences.<sup id="cite_ref-licences_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-licences-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The UEFA Pro Licence is required by every person who wishes to manage a club in the Premier League on a permanent basis (<i>i.e.</i>, more than 12 weeks, the amount of time an unqualified <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_manager" title="Caretaker manager">caretaker manager</a> is allowed to take control).<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Caretaker appointments are managers that fill the gap between a managerial departure and a new appointment. Several caretaker managers have gone on to secure a permanent managerial post after performing well as a caretaker, including <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hart" title="Paul Hart">Paul Hart</a> at <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Pleat" title="David Pleat">David Pleat</a> at <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a> is the longest-serving manager, having been in charge of <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> in the Premier League from 1996 to his retirement at the conclusion of the 2017–18 season, and holds the record for most matches managed in the Premier League with 828, all with Arsenal. He broke the record set by <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Alex Ferguson</a>, who had managed 810 matches with Manchester United from the Premier League's inception to his retirement at the end of the 2012–13 season. Ferguson was in charge of Manchester United from November 1986 until his retirement at the end of the 2012–13 season, meaning he was manager for the last five years of the old Football League First Division and all of the first 21 seasons of the Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 2019–20 season, 1 manager has been sacked as of 7 September, the most recent being <a href="/wiki/Javi_Gracia" title="Javi Gracia">Javi Gracia</a> of <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>.
</p><p>There have been several studies into the reasoning behind, and effects of, managerial sackings. Most famously, Professor Sue Bridgewater of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Liverpool" title="University of Liverpool">University of Liverpool</a> and Dr. Bas ter Weel of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Amsterdam" title="University of Amsterdam">University of Amsterdam</a>, performed two separate studies which helped to explain the statistics behind managerial sackings. Bridgewater's study found clubs generally sack their managers upon dropping below an average of one point per match.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_players_and_transfer_regulations">Foreign players and transfer regulations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_foreign_Premier_League_players" title="List of foreign Premier League players">List of foreign Premier League players</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_foreign_Premier_League_goalscorers" title="List of foreign Premier League goalscorers">List of foreign Premier League goalscorers</a></div>
<p>At the inception of the Premier League in <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_FA_Premier_League" title="1992–93 FA Premier League">1992–93</a>, just 11 players named in the starting line-ups for the first round of matches hailed from outside of the United Kingdom or Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> By <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_FA_Premier_League" title="2000–01 FA Premier League">2000–01</a>, the number of foreign players participating in the Premier League was 36% of the total. In the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_FA_Premier_League" title="2004–05 FA Premier League">2004–05</a> season, the figure had increased to 45%. On 26 December 1999, Chelsea became the first Premier League side to field an entirely foreign starting line-up,<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> and on 14 February 2005, Arsenal were the first to name a completely foreign 16-man squad for a match.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> By 2009, under 40% of the players in the Premier League were English.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In response to concerns that clubs were increasingly passing over young English players in favour of foreign players, in 1999, the <a href="/wiki/Home_Office" title="Home Office">Home Office</a> tightened its rules for granting work permits to players from countries outside of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> A non-EU player applying for the permit must have played for his country in at least 75&#160;per&#160;cent of its competitive 'A' team matches for which he was available for selection during the previous two years, and his country must have averaged at least 70th place in the official FIFA world rankings over the previous two years. If a player does not meet those criteria, the club wishing to sign him may appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-HOworkpermits_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HOworkpermits-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Players may only be <a href="/wiki/Transfer_(association_football)" title="Transfer (association football)">transferred</a> during <a href="/wiki/Transfer_window" title="Transfer window">transfer windows</a> that are set by the Football Association. The two transfer windows run from the last day of the season to 31 August and from 31 December to 31 January. Player registrations cannot be exchanged outside these windows except under specific licence from the FA, usually on an emergency basis.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> As of the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Premier_League" title="2010–11 Premier League">2010–11 season</a>, the Premier League introduced new rules mandating that each club must register a maximum 25-man squad of players aged over 21, with the squad list only allowed to be changed in transfer windows or in exceptional circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-PLHomeGrownPlayerRules16Jul2010_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PLHomeGrownPlayerRules16Jul2010-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC27July2010NewRules_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC27July2010NewRules-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> This was to enable the "home grown" rule to be enacted, whereby the Premier League would also from 2010 require at least eight members of the named 25-man squad to be "home-grown players".<sup id="cite_ref-PLHomeGrownPlayerRules16Jul2010_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PLHomeGrownPlayerRules16Jul2010-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Player_wages">Player wages</span></h3>
<p>There is no team or individual salary cap in the Premier League. As a result of the increasingly lucrative television deals, player wages rose sharply following the formation of the Premier League when the average player wage was £75,000 per year.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> In the 2018–19 season the average annual salary stood at £2.99&#160;million.
</p><p>The total salary bill for the 20 Premier League clubs in the 2018–19 was £1.62bn, this compares to £1.05bn in <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a>, £0.83bn in <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a>, £0.72bn in <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>, and £0.54bn in <a href="/wiki/Ligue_1" title="Ligue 1">Ligue 1</a>. The club with the highest average wages is <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a> at £6.5m. This is smaller than the club with the highest wage bill in Spain (<a href="/wiki/F.C._Barcelona" class="mw-redirect" title="F.C. Barcelona">Barcelona</a> £10.5m), and Italy (<a href="/wiki/Juventus" class="mw-redirect" title="Juventus">Juventus</a> £6.7m), but higher than in Germany (<a href="/wiki/Bayern_Munich" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> £6.4m), and France (<a href="/wiki/Paris_St_Germain" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris St Germain">Paris St Germain</a> 6.1m).
</p><p>The ratio of the wages of the highest paid team to lowest paid in the Premier League is 6.82 to 1. This is much lower than in <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> (19.1 to 1), <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> (16 to 1), <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> (20.5 to 1), and <a href="/wiki/Ligue_1" title="Ligue 1">Ligue 1</a> (26.6 to 1). Because of the lower differential between team wage bills in the Premier League, it is often regarded as being more competitive than other top European leagues.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Player_transfer_fees">Player transfer fees</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Progression_of_British_football_transfer_fee_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Progression of British football transfer fee record">Progression of British football transfer fee record</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_association_football_transfers" title="List of most expensive association football transfers">List of most expensive association football transfers</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Progression_of_British_football_transfer_fee_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Progression of British football transfer fee record">record transfer fee</a> for a Premier League player has risen steadily over the lifetime of the competition. Prior to the start of the first Premier League season <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a> became the first British player to command a transfer fee of more than £3&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-OSMtransfers_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSMtransfers-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The record has increased steadily and <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Coutinho" title="Philippe Coutinho">Philippe Coutinho</a> is now the most expensive transfer involving a Premier League club at £106&#160;million. The highest transfer fee paid by a Premier League club is £89&#160;million for <a href="/wiki/Paul_Pogba" title="Paul Pogba">Paul Pogba</a>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Top_scorers">Top scorers</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_footballers_with_100_or_more_Premier_League_goals" title="List of footballers with 100 or more Premier League goals">List of footballers with 100 or more Premier League goals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Top_Premier_League_goal_scorers_by_season" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Premier League goal scorers by season">Top Premier League goal scorers by season</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alan_Shearer_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Alan_Shearer_2008.jpg/170px-Alan_Shearer_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Alan_Shearer_2008.jpg/255px-Alan_Shearer_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Alan_Shearer_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="303" data-file-height="422" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alan_Shearer_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a> is the top scorer in Premier League history.</div></div></div>

<p><small><i>Italics</i> denotes players still playing professional football,<br /><b>Bold</b> denotes players still playing in the Premier League.</small>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Golden Boot</a> is awarded to the top Premier League scorer at the end of each season. Former Blackburn Rovers and <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> striker <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a> holds the record for most Premier League goals with 260.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_players_with_100_or_more_goals" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Premier League players with 100 or more goals">Twenty-eight players</a> have reached the 100-goal mark.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
Since the first Premier League season in 1992–93, 14 players from 10 clubs have won or shared the top scorers title.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a> won his fourth overall scoring title by scoring 27 goals in the 2005–06 season. <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Cole" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrew Cole">Andrew Cole</a> and Alan Shearer hold the record for most goals in a season (34) – for Newcastle and Blackburn respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a> of Manchester United holds the record for scoring goals in consecutive seasons, having scored in the first 21 seasons of the league.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trophy">Trophy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Premiership_trophy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f0/Premiership_trophy.jpg/170px-Premiership_trophy.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f0/Premiership_trophy.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="228" data-file-height="435" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Premiership_trophy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Premier League trophy</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GoldInvinciblesTrophy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/GoldInvinciblesTrophy.jpg/170px-GoldInvinciblesTrophy.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/GoldInvinciblesTrophy.jpg/255px-GoldInvinciblesTrophy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/GoldInvinciblesTrophy.jpg/340px-GoldInvinciblesTrophy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GoldInvinciblesTrophy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The gold Premier League trophy awarded to <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> for winning the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="2003–04 Premier League">2003–04</a> title without defeat</div></div></div>
<p>The Premier League maintains two trophies – the genuine trophy (held by the reigning champions) and a spare replica. Two trophies are held in the event that two clubs could win the League on the final day of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> In the rare event that more than two clubs are vying for the title on the final day of the season – then a replica won by a previous club is used.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The current Premier League trophy was created by Royal Jewellers <a href="/wiki/Garrard_%26_Co" title="Garrard &amp; Co">Asprey of London</a>. It consists of a trophy with a golden crown and a <a href="/wiki/Malachite" title="Malachite">malachite</a> plinth base. The plinth weighs 33 pounds (15&#160;kg) and the trophy weighs 22 pounds (10.0&#160;kg).<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> The trophy and plinth are 76&#160;cm (30&#160;in) tall, 43&#160;cm (17&#160;in) wide and 25&#160;cm (9.8&#160;in) deep.<sup id="cite_ref-Trophy_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trophy-230">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Its main body is solid <a href="/wiki/Sterling_silver" title="Sterling silver">sterling silver</a> and silver <a href="/wiki/Gilding" title="Gilding">gilt</a>, while its plinth is made of malachite, a <a href="/wiki/Semi-precious" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-precious">semi-precious</a> stone. The plinth has a silver band around its circumference, upon which the names of the title-winning clubs are listed. Malachite's green colour is also representative of the green field of play.<sup id="cite_ref-Trophy_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trophy-230">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> The design of the trophy is based on the <a href="/wiki/Heraldry" title="Heraldry">heraldry</a> of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Arms_of_England" title="Royal Arms of England">Three Lions</a> that is associated with English football. Two of the lions are found above the handles on either side of the trophy – the third is symbolised by the captain of the title-winning team as he raises the trophy, and its gold crown, above his head at the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> The ribbons that drape the handles are presented in the team colours of the league champions that year. In 2004, a special gold version of the trophy was commissioned to commemorate Arsenal winning the title <a href="/wiki/The_Invincibles_(football)" title="The Invincibles (football)">without a single defeat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Player_and_manager_awards">Player and manager awards</span></h3>
<p>In addition to the winner's trophy and the individual <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_winning_players" title="List of Premier League winning players">winner's medals</a> awarded to players who win the title, the Premier League also issues other awards throughout the season.
</p><p>A man of the match award is awarded to the player who has the greatest impact in an individual match.
</p><p>Monthly awards are also given for the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Manager_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Manager of the Month">Manager of the Month</a>, <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Player of the Month</a> and <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Goal_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Goal of the Month">Goal of the Month</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> These are also issued annually for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Manager_of_the_Season" title="Premier League Manager of the Season">Manager of the Season</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Season" title="Premier League Player of the Season">Player of the Season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-poty2010_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poty2010-235">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Goal_of_the_Season" title="Premier League Goal of the Season">Goal of the Season</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Golden Boot</a> award is given to the top goalscorer of every season, The <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Playmaker_of_the_Season" title="Premier League Playmaker of the Season">Playmaker of the Season</a> award is given to the player who make the most assists of every season<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Glove" title="Premier League Golden Glove">Golden Glove</a> award is given to the goalkeeper with the most clean sheets at the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Premier_League" title="2017–18 Premier League">2017–18 season</a>, players also receive a milestone award for 100 appearances and every century there after and also players who score 50 goals and multiples thereof. Each player to reach these milestones will receive a presentation box from the Premier League containing a special medallion and a plaque commemorating their achievement.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20_Seasons_Awards">20 Seasons Awards</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Premier League 20 Seasons Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_10_Seasons_Awards" title="Premier League 10 Seasons Awards">Premier League 10 Seasons Awards</a></div>
<p>In 2012, the Premier League celebrated its second decade by holding the 20 Seasons Awards:<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards#Fantasy_Teams_of_the_20_Seasons" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Fantasy Team of the 20 Seasons</a>
<ul><li><b>Panel Choice:</b> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Schmeichel" title="Peter Schmeichel">Peter Schmeichel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Neville" title="Gary Neville">Gary Neville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Adams_(footballer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tony Adams (footballer)">Tony Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Ferdinand" title="Rio Ferdinand">Rio Ferdinand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Cole" title="Ashley Cole">Ashley Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roy_Keane" title="Roy Keane">Roy Keane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Scholes" title="Paul Scholes">Paul Scholes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a></li>
<li><b>Public Vote:</b> Peter Schmeichel, Gary Neville, Tony Adams, <a href="/wiki/Nemanja_Vidi%C4%87" title="Nemanja Vidić">Nemanja Vidić</a>, Ashley Cole, Cristiano Ronaldo, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a>, Paul Scholes, Ryan Giggs, Thierry Henry, Alan Shearer</li></ul></li></ul>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards#Best_Manager" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Best Manager</a>: <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Sir Alex Ferguson</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards#Best_Player" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Best Player</a>: <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards#Other_statistical_recognitions" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Most Appearances</a>: <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Barry" title="Gareth Barry">Gareth Barry</a> (652)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards#Other_statistical_recognitions" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Top Goalscorer</a>: <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a> (260)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards#Other_statistical_recognitions" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Most Clean Sheets</a>: <a href="/wiki/David_James_(footballer)" class="mw-redirect" title="David James (footballer)">David James</a> (173)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards#Other_statistical_recognitions" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">500 Club</a>: <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Carragher" title="Jamie Carragher">Jamie Carragher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Barry" title="Gareth Barry">Gareth Barry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_James_(footballer)" class="mw-redirect" title="David James (footballer)">David James</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Speed" title="Gary Speed">Gary Speed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emile_Heskey" title="Emile Heskey">Emile Heskey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sol_Campbell" title="Sol Campbell">Sol Campbell</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards#Best_Goal" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Best Goal</a>: <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a>, 12 February 2011, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Man. United</a> vs <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Man. City</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards#Best_Save" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Best Save</a>: <a href="/wiki/Craig_Gordon" title="Craig Gordon">Craig Gordon</a>, 18 December 2010, <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> vs <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Premier_League_20_Seasons_Awards#Best_Team" title="Premier League 20 Seasons Awards">Best Team</a>: <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Arsenal_F.C._season" title="2003–04 Arsenal F.C. season">2003–04 Arsenal</a></li></ul>
</div>
